## Page 258

E1 
1. 
PURPOSE AND APPLICATION 
 
The purpose of this laboratory procedure is to provide dummy users (independent testing 
laboratories under contract with the Office of Crashworthiness Standards) with standard test 
procedures for performing receiving-inspection and performance qualification tests on the 
Part 572, Subpart R dummy so that repetitive and correlative test results can be obtained. The 
following tests have been developed to establish a uniform qualification procedure for all users as 
the means of verifying the performance of the dummy. 
 
 
A. 
EXTERNAL DIMENSIONS (PADI) 
 
 
B. 
HEAD DROP TEST (572.152) 
 
 
C. 
NECK FLEXION TEST (572.153(b)(1)) 
 
 
D. 
NECK EXTENSION TEST 572.153(b)(2) 
 
 
E. 
THORAX IMPACT TEST ((572.154) 
 
National Highway Traffic Safety Administration (NHTSA) contract laboratories performing 
NCAP testing for the Office of Crashworthiness Standards (OCWS) must use this laboratory 
procedure for the qualification of Part 572, Subpart R dummies. 
 
2. 
GENERAL REQUIREMENTS 
 
The Code of Federal Regulations (49CFR), Parts 571 and 572, was amended to adopt the Hybrid 
III, CRABI 12-Month-Old Dummy as the means of determining a vehicle's conformance to the 
performance requirements of FMVSS 208. Each Part 572, Subpart R dummy used in an NCAP 
test must meet the specifications and performance criteria of Part 572 before and after each 
vehicle crash test in order to be an acceptable test tool. 
 
The Part 572, Subpart R Hybrid III, CRABI 12-Month-Old Dummy consists of components and 
assemblies specified in the drawing and specifications package which is available from 
www.regulations.gov (search Docket No. NHTSA-2000- 7052). 
 
3. 
SECURITY 
 
 
All NHTSA Part 572, Subpart R test dummies delivered to the contract laboratory as 
Government Furnished Property (GFP) will be stored in a safe and secure area such as a 
dummy qualification laboratory. The contractor is financially responsible for any acts of 
theft and/or vandalism that occur during the storage of GFP. Any security problems shall 
be reported by telephone to the Industrial Property Manager (IPM), Office of Contracts 
and Procurement, within two working days after the incident. A letter containing specific 
details of the security problem will be sent to the IPM (with copy to the COR) within 48 
hours. 
 
The contractor is responsible for maintaining the NHTSA test dummies in good working 
order, and shall protect and segregate the data that evolves from conducting Part 572, 
Subpart R dummy qualification tests before and after each vehicle test usage. 


## Page 259

E2 
 
No Information concerning the Part 572, Subpart R dummy qualification data shall be 
released to anyone except the COR, unless specifically authorized by the COR or the 
COR's Branch or Division Chief. 
 
NOTE: No individuals, other than contractor personnel directly involved in 
the dummy qualification test program, shall be allowed to witness 
dummy qualification tests unless specifically authorized by the COR. 
 
4. 
GOOD HOUSEKEEPING 
 
Contractors shall maintain the entire dummy qualification laboratory, test fixtures, and 
instrumentation in a neat, clean, and painted condition with test instruments arranged in 
an orderly manner consistent with good test laboratory housekeeping practices. 
 
5. 
TEST SCHEDULING AND MONITORING 
 
The Part 572, Subpart R dummies are being qualified as test tools to be used in NCAP 
vehicle crash tests. The schedule for these performance qualification tests must be 
correlated with that of the vehicle tests. All testing shall be coordinated to allow 
monitoring by the COR. 
 
6. 
TEST DATA DISPOSITION 
 
The contractor shall make all dummy qualification data available to the COR for review 
and analysis as required. All qualification test data for each particular Part 572, Subpart R 
dummy will be sent to the COR with each test report. 
 
All backup data sheets, strip charts, recordings, plots, technicians’ notes, etc. shall be 
either sent to the COR or destroyed at the conclusion of each delivery order, purchase 
order, etc. 
 
7. 
GOVERNMENT FURNISHED PROPERTY (GFP) 
 
Part 572, Subpart R test dummies will be furnished to the contract laboratory by the 
OCWS. The dummies shall be stored in a hanging position using the bracket and 
positioning shown in drawings 1E and 2E. 


## Page 260

E3 
 
FIGURE 1E 
 
 


## Page 261

E4 
 
FIGURE 2E


## Page 262

E5 
These dummies shall be stored in a secured room that is kept between 55ºF and 85ºF. The 
contractor will check dummy components for damage after each crash test and complete 
a dummy damage checklist (as part of the NCAP procedure), which will be included with 
the dummy qualification, if requested. The COR will be kept informed of the dummies’ 
condition so that replacement parts can be provided. The dummies will be qualified by 
the contractor according to the schedule indicated in the NCAP test procedure. 
 
 
8. 
CALIBRATION AND TEST INSTRUMENTATION 
 
Before the contractor initiates the dummy performance qualification test program, a test 
instrumentation calibration system must be implemented and maintained in accordance 
with established calibration practices. The calibration system shall be set up and 
maintained as follows: 
 
A. 
Standards for calibrating the measuring and test equipment shall be stored and 
used under appropriate environmental conditions to assure their accuracy and 
stability. 
 
B. 
All measuring instruments and standards shall be calibrated by the contractor, or a 
commercial facility, against a higher order standard at periodic intervals not 
exceeding 12 months for instruments and 12 months for calibration standards. 
Records, showing the calibration traceability to the National Institute of Standards 
and Technology (NIST), shall be maintained for all measuring and test 
equipment. 
 
C. 
All measuring and test equipment and measuring standards shall be labeled with 
the following information: 
 
1. Date of calibration 
 
2. Date of next scheduled calibration 
 
3. Name of the technician who calibrated the equipment 
 
D. 
The contractor shall provide a written calibration procedure that includes, as a 
minimum, the following information for all measurement and test equipment: 
 
1. Type of equipment, manufacturer, model number, etc. 
 
2. Measurement range 
 
3. Accuracy 
 
4. Calibration interval 
 


## Page 263

E6 
5. Type of standard used to calibrate the equipment (calibration traceability of 
the standard must be evident) 
 
6. The actual procedures and forms used to perform calibrations 
 
E. 
The contractor shall keep records of calibrations for all test instrumentation in a 
manner that assures the maintenance of established calibration schedules. All such 
records shall be readily available for inspection when requested by the COR. The 
calibration system will need the written acceptance of the COR before testing 
begins. 
 
F. 
Test equipment shall receive a calibration check immediately prior to and after 
each test. This check shall be recorded by the test technician(s) and submitted 
with the final report. 
 
G. 
Anthropomorphic test devices shall be qualified as indicated in NCAP test 
procedure. These qualifications shall be submitted with the final report. 
 
9. 
PHOTOGRAPHIC DOCUMENTATION 
 
Provide still photographs (color prints properly focused for clear images, no more than 
two (2) per 8.5”x11” sheet) of post-test damage resulting from the vehicle crash test. 
 
10. 
DEFINITIONS 
 
 
PADI: Procedures for Assembly, Disassembly, and Inspection 
 
11. 
PRE-TEST REQUIREMENTS 
 
11.1 
TRANSDUCER REQUIREMENTS 
 
The contractor shall provide and install the following instrumentation to the GFP 
dummies (excluding the chest deflection transducer). 
 
A. 
HEAD – The head accelerometers shall have dimensions, response characteristics 
and sensitive mass locations specified in drawing SA572-S4 and be mounted in 
the head as shown in drawing 921022-000. (572.155(b)) 
 
Three accelerometers shall be mounted in the head cavity to measure orthogonal 
accelerations (Ax, Ay, Az) at the center of gravity (CG) of the head assembly. 
 
B. 
NECK – The neck force-moment transducer shall have the dimensions, response 
characteristics, and sensitive axis locations specified in drawing SA572-S23 and 
shall be mounted as shown in drawing 921022-000. (572.155(c)) 
 


## Page 264

E7 
C. 
CHEST – The chest accelerometers shall have the dimensions, response 
characteristics, and sensitive mass locations specified in drawing SA572-S4 and 
be mounted in the torso assembly in triaxial configuration at the T4 location as 
shown drawing 921022-000. The chest accelerometers are not required for 
dummy qualification testing but may be required for NCAP testing. (572.155(e)) 
 
D. 
TEST FIXTURE – The neck pendulum and thorax accelerometers shall have the 
dimensions and characteristics of drawing SA572-S4. 
 
11.2 
OTHER TRANSDUCER CONDITIONS 
 
A. 
TRANSDUCER MOUNTS – The mountings for sensing devices shall have no 
resonance frequency less than 3 times the frequency range of the applicable 
channel class. (572.155(k)) 
 
B. 
TRANSDUCER SIGN CONVENTION - The sign convention for outputs of 
transducers mounted within the dummy that measure head and chest 
accelerations, chest deflection and neck loads are located in Figure 3E. For other 
transducers see SAE J1733DEC94. (572.155(i)) 
 
C. 
TRANSDUCER OUTPUT FILTERING - The outputs of acceleration and 
force-sensing devices installed in the dummy and in the test apparatus specified 
by this part are recorded with individual data channels. Each data channel will be 
comprised of a sensor, signal conditioner, data acquisition device, and all 
interconnecting cables, and must conform to the requirements of SAE 
Recommended Practice J211/1 MAR95, "Instrumentation for Impact Test," with 
channel classes as follows: (572.155(i)) 
 
1. Head acceleration  
 
Class 1000 
(572.155(i)(1)) 
2. Neck force  
 
 
Class 1000 
(572.155(i)(2)(i)) 
3. Neck moment 
 
 
Class 600 
(572.155(i)(2)(ii)) 
4. Neck pendulum acceleration 
Class 180 
(572.155(i)(2)(iii)) 
5. Neck rotation transducers  
Class 60 
(572.155(i)(2)(iv)) 
6. Thorax spine acceleration  
Class 180 
(572.155(i)(3)(ii)) 
7. Thorax pendulum  
 
Class 180 
(572.155(i)(3)(ii)) 
acceleration 
 
All filter classes should be of the "phaseless" type to be compatible with the 
"time" dependent test parameters. 
 
11.3 
THORAX IMPACTOR PROBE (572.155(a)) 
 
A. 
The test probe for thoracic impacts shall be of rigid metallic construction, 
concentric about its longitudinal axis. 
B. 
It shall have a mass of 2.86 ± 0.02 kg (6.3 ± 0.05 lbs). 1/3 of the weight of the 
suspension cables and any attachments to the impact probe must be included in 


## Page 265

E8 
the calculation of mass, and such components may not exceed 5 percent of the 
total weight of the test probe. 
C. 
It shall have a minimum mass moment of inertia of 164 kg-cm2 (0.145 lbs-in-sec2) 
in yaw and pitch about the center of gravity. 
D. 
The impacting end of the probe is perpendicular to and concentric with the 
longitudinal axis. The face has a diameter of 101.6 ± 0.25 mm (4.00 ± 0.01 in), a 
maximum edge radius of 7.6 to 12.7 mm (0.3 to 0.5 in) and is flat, continuous and 
non-deformable. 
E. 
A 101-103 mm diameter cylinder surface extends at least 12.5 mm to the rear of 
the impact face. 
F. 
The probe’s end opposite to the impact face must have provisions for mounting of 
an accelerometer with its sensitive axis collinear with the longitudinal axis of the 
probe. 
G. 
The impact probe shall have a free air resonant frequency of not less than 1000 
Hz measured in line with the longitudinal axis of the impactor.

## Page 268

E11 
11.4 
GENERAL TEST CONDITIONS 
 
A. 
Surfaces of dummy components are not painted unless otherwise specified. 
(572.155(n)) 
 
B. 
Dummy performance tests of the same component, segment, assembly, or fully 
assembled dummy are separated in time by a period of not less than 30 minutes 
unless otherwise specified. (572.155(m)) 
 
C. 
The dummy head performance tests are conducted at any temperature from 
18.9oC (66ºF) to 25.6oC (78ºF) and at any relative humidity from 10% to 70% 
after exposure of the dummy to these conditions for a period of not less than 4 
hours. For the neck-headform assembly and thorax assembly, the temperature 
range is 20.6oC (69ºF) to 22.2oC (72ºF) and at any relative humidity from 10% to 
70% after exposure of the dummy to these conditions for a period of not less than 
4 hours. 
 
D. 
Dummy limb joints are set at 1 G, barely restraining the weight of the limb when 
it is extended horizontally. The force required to move a limb segment does not 
exceed 2 Gs throughout the range of limb motion. (572.155(l)) 
 
E. 
Dummies will be clothed for the thorax qualification tests with a form fitting 
cotton-polyester-based tight-fitting sweat shirt with long sleeves and ankle length 
pants. The total weight of the shirt and pants shall not exceed 0.25 kg (0.55 lb). 
(572.154(c)(2)) 
 
12. 
QUALIFICATION TEST EXECUTION 
 
 
Complete the Data Sheets in section 15. 
 
13. 
POST-TEST REQUIREMENTS 
 
The contractor shall verify all instrumentation and check data sheets and photographs.  
Make sure data is recorded in all data blocks on every performance qualification test data 
sheet. 
 
14. 
REPORTS 
 
14.1 
APPARENT NONCONFORMANCE 
 
During a qualification verification, any indication of apparent nonconformance to the 
requirements of Regulation P572 shall be communicated by telephone to the COR within 
24 hours with written notification mailed within 48 hours (Saturdays and Sundays 
excluded). Written notification shall be submitted with a copy of the particular test data 
sheet(s) and preliminary data plot(s). 
 


## Page 269

E12 
In the event of an apparent nonconformance, a calibration check of some critically 
sensitive test equipment and instrumentation may be required for verification of accuracy. 
The necessity for the calibration shall be at the COR's discretion and shall be performed 
without additional costs to the OCWS. 
 
14.2 
FINAL PERFORMANCE QUALIFICATION REPORTS 
 
14.2.1 COPIES 
 
A report containing the qualification data for each Part 572, Subpart R dummy used in 
the vehicle crash test shall be submitted with the final NCAP test report for the vehicle. 
 
Contractors are required to PROOF READ all Final Test Reports before submittal to the 
COR. The OCWS will not act as a report quality control office for contractors. Reports 
containing a significant number of errors will be returned to the contractor for correction, 
and a "hold" will be placed on invoice payment for the particular test.

DATA SHEET E2 
EXTERNAL MEASUREMENTS (12-MONTH-OLD)   
(See the PADI) 
 
Dummy Serial Number _________________ 
 
 
Test Date _____________ 
Technician ___________________________ 
 
__Pre-test qualification 
__Post-test qualification verification 
 
__1. 
Seat the dummy on a flat, rigid, smooth, clean, dry, horizontal surface. The seating 
surface is at least 406 mm (16 in) wide and 221 mm (8 11/16 in) in depth with a vertical 
section at least 406 mm (16 in) wide and 610 mm (24 in) high attached to the rear of the 
seating fixture. The dummy's midsagittal plane is vertical and centered on the test 
surface. 
__2. 
Secure the dummy to the test fixture so that the upper torso and buttocks are tangent to 
the rear vertical surface of the fixture (as tangent as possible). 
__3. 
Push the dummy’s forehead rearward and secure the head (at the forehead) against the 
seat back surface. 
__4. 
Place the centerlines of the upper arms vertical. 
__5. 
Place the centerlines of the lower arms horizontal. 
__6. 
Position the upper legs so that they are parallel to one another. 
__7. 
Position the lower legs so that they are perpendicular to the upper legs and the bottom of 
the foot is horizontal. 
__8. 
Record the dimensions listed in following table, except for dimension Q (reference 
Figure 4E). 
__9. 
Place the dummy in supine position on the measurement surface. Place a block that is 
perpendicular to the table at both the head and feet of the dummy. Position the blocks 
perpendicular to the midsagittal plane of the dummy. Position the blocks so they are in 
contact with the head and the heels of the dummy. Measure the distance between the 
blocks for Q.

__9. 
Install the transducers or other devices for measuring the "D" plane rotation with respect 
to the pendulum longitudinal centerline. Note: Plane "D" is the top horizontal surface of 
the neck load cell. These measurement devices should be designed to minimize their 
influence upon the performance of the head-neck assembly and not induce neck torsion. 
(572.153(c)(3)(ii)) 
__10. Plane D is perpendicular ± 1 degree to the centerline of the pendulum. 


## Page 286

E29 
__11. Set the instrumentation so that the moment and rotation are defined to be zero when the 
longitudinal centerline of the neck and pendulum are parallel. (572.153(c)(3)(i)) 
__12. Release the pendulum and allow it to fall freely from a height to achieve an impact speed 
of 2.4 m/s to 2.6 m/s as measured at the center of the pendulum accelerometer at the 
instant of contact with the honeycomb. (572.153(c)(4))

__5. 
Seat the dummy, without back support on the test fixture surface as shown in Figure 
10E. The legs are extended forward, parallel to the midsagittal plane. The surface must 
be long enough to support the pelvis and outstretched legs. (572.154(c)(3)) 
__6.

material may be used under the upper legs to maintain the dummy’s specified spine box

The longitudinal centerline of the test probe is centered within ±2.5 mm of the 
midsagittal plane, 196 ± 2.5 mm vertically from the plane of the seating surface and is 
within ±0.5º of a horizontal line in the dummy's midsagittal plane. (572.154(c)(4)) 
__10. The data acquisition system, including transducers, must conform to the requirements of 
SAE Recommended Practice J211/1 MAR95 (572.146(l)). 
__11. Impact the anterior surface of the thorax with the test probe so the longitudinal centerline 
of the probe is within 2º of a horizontal line in the dummy's midsagittal plane at the 
moment of impact. (572.154(c)(5)) The velocity of the test probe at the time of impact is 
between 4.9 m/s and 5.1 m/s. (572.154(b)) The probe is guided so there is no significant 
lateral, vertical or rotational movement during the impact. (572.154(c)(6) Neither the 
suspension hardware, suspension cables, nor other attachments to the probe, including the 
velocity vane, make contact with the dummy. (572.154(c)(7)

Probe specifications: 
1. 
Rigid metallic construction and concentric about its longitudinal axis. 
2. 
A mass of 2.86 ± 0.02 kg (6.3 ± 0.05 lbs). 1/3 of the weight of the suspension cables and their attachments 
to the impact probe are included in the calculation of mass, and such components may not exceed 5 percent 
of the total weight of the test probe. 
3. 
Minimum mass moment of inertia of 164 kg-cm2 (0.145 lbs-in-sec2) in yaw and pitch about the center of 
gravity. 
4. 
The impacting end of the probe is perpendicular to and concentric with the longitudinal axis. It has a flat, 
continuous, and non-deformable face with diameter of 101.6 ± 0.25 mm (4.00 ± 0.01 in) and an edge radius 
of 7.6 to 12.7 mm (0.3 to 0.5 in.). 
5. 
A 101-103 mm (4.0-4.1 in) diameter cylinder surface extends at least 12.5 mm to the rear of the impact 
face. 
6. 
The probe’s end opposite to the impact face must have provisions for mounting of an accelerometer with its 
sensitive axis collinear with the longitudinal axis of the probe. 
7. 
The impact probe shall have a free air resonant frequency of not less than 1000 Hz in line with the 
longitudinal axis of the impactor.

1. 
Seating and Positioning/DATA SHEET 1: Hybrid III 50th Male, Driver 
Part 572, Subpart E, all section references refer to FMVSS No. 208 
 
__1. Position the seat’s adjustable lumbar supports so that the lumbar support is in its lowest, 
retracted or deflated adjustment position. (S8.1.3) 
__N/A – No lumbar adjustment 
 
__2. Position any adjustable parts of the seat that provide additional support so that they are in 
the lowest or most open adjustment position. (S16.2.10.2) 
__ N/A – No additional support adjustment 
 
__3. Use all the seat controls that have any effect on the fore-aft movement of the seat to move 
the seat cushion to the rearmost position. Mark this position. (8/31/95 legal interp to Hogan and 
Hartson) 
 
__4. Use all the seat controls that have any effect on the fore-aft movement of the seat to move 
the seat cushion to the foremost position. Mark this position. (8/31/95 legal interp to Hogan and 
Hartson) 
 
__5. Mark each fore-aft position so that there is a visual indication when the seat is at a 
particular position. For manual seats, mark each detent. For power seats, mark only the 
rearmost, middle, and foremost positions. Label three of the positions with the following: F for 
foremost, M for mid-position (if there is no mid-position, label the closest adjustment position to 
the rear of the mid-point), and R for rearmost. Determine the mid fore-aft seat position based on 
the foremost and rearmost positions determined in items 3 and 4. (8/31/95 legal interp to Hogan 
and Hartson) 
 
__6. Move the seat to the mid position. 
 
__7. While maintaining the mid position, move the seat to its lowest position. Mark the height 
position. For seats with adjustable seat cushions, use the manufacturer’s recommended seat 
cushion angle for determining the lowest height position.

surface. (S10.4.1.1)

2. 
Seating and Positioning/DATA SHEET 2: Hybrid III 5th Female, Front Passenger  
Part 572, Subpart O, all section references refer to FMVSS No. 208 
 
(Check this item ONLY if it applies to this vehicle.) 
__The passenger seat adjustments are controlled by the adjustments made to the driver’s 
seat. Therefore, positioning of the passenger dummy is made simultaneously with the 
driver dummy. Adjustments made to the seat to position the driver will override any 
adjustments that would normally be made to position the passenger. (S16.2.10.3) 
 
1. Seat Position 
__1.1 Position the seat’s adjustable lumbar supports so that the lumbar supports are in the lowest, 
retracted or deflated adjustment positions. (S16.2.10.1, S20.1.9.1, S20.4.1, 
S22.1.7.1) 
__ N/A – No lumbar adjustment 
__1.2 Position any adjustable parts of the seat that provide additional support so that they are in 
the lowest or most open adjustment position. (S16.2.10.2, S20.1.9.2, S20.4.1, 
S22.1.7.1, S22.4.2.1, S22.4.3.1, S24.4.2.1, S26.2.3, S26.3.1) 
__ N/A – No additional support adjustment

to Toyota) 
__N/A – No adjustable leg support system 
__1.4 Mark a point (seat cushion reference point) on the side of the seat cushion that is between 
150 mm and 250 mm from the front edge of the seat cushion. (S16.3.1.12) 
__1.5 Draw a line (seat cushion reference line) through the seat cushion reference point. 
(S16.3.1.13) 
__1.6 Use only the controls that primarily move the seat in the fore-aft direction to move the seat 
cushion reference point to the rearmost position. (S16.2.10.3.1, S22.1.7.3) 
__1.7 If the seat cushion adjusts fore-aft, independent of the seat back, use only the controls that 
primarily move the seat cushion in the fore-aft direction to move the seat cushion 
reference point to the rearmost position. (S16.2.10.3.1, S20.1.9.3) 
__ N/A – No independent fore-aft seat cushion adjustment

2. Head Restraint Position

__2.1 Adjust the head restraint to its lowest position. (S16.2.10.2, S20.1.9.6 S20.4.1, S22.1.7.6, 
S22.4.2.1, S22.4.3.1, S24.4.3.1, S26.2.3, S26.3.1) 
__2.2 All adjustments of the head restraint shall be used to position it full forward. For example, 
if it rotates, rotate it such that the head restraint extends as far forward as possible. Mark the 
foremost position. (S16.2.10.2 & S16.3.4.4 & S20.1.9.6, S20.4.1, S22.4.2.1, S22.4.3.1, 
S24.4.3.1, S26.2.3, S26.3.1) 
__2.3 Measure the vertical distance from the top most point of the head restraint to the bottom 
most point. Locate and mark a horizontal plane through the midpoint of this distance.

1. PURPOSE AND APPLICATION 
 
The New Car Assessment Program’s (NCAP’s) full frontal rigid barrier impact test procedure is 
based on a related safety standard, Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standard (FMVSS) No. 208, 
which specifies performance requirements for the protection of vehicle occupants in crashes.  
 
This document is an appendix to the main full frontal rigid barrier laboratory test procedure 
provided by the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration (NHTSA), Office of 
Crashworthiness Standards (OCWS) for the purpose of presenting guidelines for a uniform 
testing data and information recording format, and providing suggestions for the use of related 
Anthropomorphic Test Device (ATD) equipment for contracted testing laboratories. The data are 
gathered from instrumentation that may be used when testing with certain Hybrid III frontal test 
dummies. The OCWS test procedure is not intended to limit or restrain a contractor from 
developing or utilizing any testing techniques or equipment that will assist in procuring the 
required test data. However, applicability of any such testing technique or equipment is subject 
to prior approval by the COR. 
 
The requirements presented in this appendix are applicable to ATDs equipped with one or more 
of the following types of instrumentation while tested under the main full frontal NCAP test 
procedure: 
 
• Redundant Instrumentation 
• Nine Axis Accelerometers 
• Angular Rate Sensors 
• Upper and Lower Neck Load Cells 
• Foot Accelerometers 
 
It is the contractor’s responsibility to follow the most updated versions of all related test 
procedures when using test devices equipped with the following instrumentation.  
 
2. GENERAL REQUIREMENTS 
 
This laboratory test procedure provides guidelines for the use of various Hybrid III ATD 
instrumentation used during full frontal NCAP tests. There may be no minimum performance 
requirements or any Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standard (FMVSS)-related requirements 
associated with the information collected, however, visual inspection of a dummy’s parts per the 
qualification procedure is still required. 
 
2.1 SAE J211 
 
Standardized coordinate systems and recorded polarities for various transducer outputs relative 
to positive directions of those coordinate systems are defined for crash test dummies, vehicle 
structures, and laboratory fixtures in the SAE J211 standard. A standardized coordinate system 
and polarities for data permits comparison of data from different crash test facilities. 
 
NHTSA requires that the polarity of any instrumentation channel be compatible with and 


## Page 309

G3 
recordable in accordance with SAE J211. A channel, by definition, includes all the 
instrumentation from the transducer to the data acquisition system output, including connectors, 
wiring, data acquisition software and hardware. 
 
2.2 SAE J1733 
 
SAE J1733 explains that for any dummy component oriented in its standard position blows to the 
back side, left side, and top will produce positive accelerations relative to its +x, +y, and +z 
directions, respectfully. 
 
One technique to document the polarity of the accelerometers is to apply blows to the dummy’s 
head with a rubber mallet (never apply the blow directly to an accelerometer mount) and record 
the data channel output. Figure G1 illustrates this technique, including the directions of expected 
positive polarity. 
 
 
Figure G1: Head Impact Directions that Produce Positive Accelerations Relative to the 
Head Coordinate System 
 
For example, to document the polarity of the x-axis accelerometer data channel, apply a blow to 
the back of the head. The polarity of the head x dummy channel should be positive as in Figure 
G2 and no changes are needed to conform to the sign convention. Similarly, when applying 
blows to the left side and top of the head with a rubber mallet, the polarity of the dummy’s y and 
z-axis accelerometer data channels should be positive. 


## Page 310

G4 
 
Figure G2: Response of x-axis accelerometer data channel from blow to rear of head 
showing desired positive polarity 
 
Figure G3 illustrates a negative output from a blow to the left side of the dummy’s head, which 
is the incorrect polarity. In this case, the channel polarity needs to be changed to agree with the 
sign convention prior to submitting the data to NHTSA. A sign change in the software may be 
the simplest solution. 
 
 
Figure G3: Response of y-axis accelerometer data channel from blow to left side of head 
showing incorrect negative polarity 
 
2.3 INFLUENCING CHANNEL POLARITY  
The polarity of a data channel for any given dummy may be affected by changing the positive 
and negative pins from the instrumentation to the wiring in a connector, the polarity assigned in 
the software, or by changing the way it is mounted in the dummy. NHTSA recommends the 
Contractor adopt standard wiring practices across similar sensor types, such that polarity can be 
verified through visual inspection of the transducer. 
 


## Page 311

G5 
Since there are many ways to influence the polarity of a data channel it is appropriate to 
document the polarity of the assembled channel upon receipt and just before testing to assure the 
instrumentation is recording data in the appropriate orientation. 
 
When a test dummy is delivered to the Contractor and connected to the data acquisition system, 
the polarity of the internal instrumentation should be determined using the following approaches. 
The procedures require manipulating various dummy body regions to determine the polarities of 
the channels in question with respect to the sign convention.  
 
NOTE: If the polarity of any instrumentation is incorrect with respect to the sign 
conventions presented below, then steps must be taken to correct it prior to submitting 
data to NHTSA.  
 
If, when properly following these procedures, channel polarity cannot be determined, it may 
indicate that the accelerometer, load cell, or other instrumentation has not been mounted in 
accordance with the assembly drawings. 
 
3. REDUNDANT INSTRUMENTATION 
 
The following guidelines are for affixing redundant accelerometers or load cells in the heads, 
chests, and femurs of the Hybrid III dummies. The Contractor is expected to closely follow these 
guidelines and shall contact the COR if difficulties arise in meeting them or if more details are 
needed. 
 
The locations of the primary instrumentation (head, chest, or femur, as specified in the test 
procedure) shall not be altered as a result of installing any redundant instrumentation. In 
addition, the center of gravity (C.G.) of the head, chest, or femur with the redundant 
instrumentation installed shall stay within the allowable range as indicated in Hybrid III 
specifications. 
 
Any weight increases due to the installation of redundant instrumentation in the heads, chests, or 
femurs shall be within the allowable weight variations specified for these body regions in Hybrid 
III drawings and/or other documentation. 
 
To simplify and facilitate the installation of accelerometers, for example, the following 
recommendations are provided: 
 
• Use of SAE572-S4 accelerometers and existing mounting fixtures is desirable 
because of their light weight. 
• Redundant SAE572-S4 accelerometers can be attached directly to the primary ones, 
either head-to-head or back-to-back. Both can then be attached to one side of the 
mounting cube. 
• The use of spacers between the primary and redundant accelerometers is 
recommended for better stability. Spacers shall be made of aluminum due to weight 
considerations. 
 


## Page 312

G6 
Any injury criterion values (HIC, 3ms chest clip, and femur loads) generated by redundant 
instrumentation shall not deviate more than ten (10) percent from the injury criterion values 
generated by their corresponding primary instrumentation. If a greater than 10 percent deviation 
is discovered during any testing, the Contractor should investigate to determine whether the 
primary or redundant instrumentation is producing an incorrect output. The COR should also be 
notified. 
 
4. HEAD ROTATIONAL INSTRUMENTATION 
These guidelines provide a practical methodology for pre-test checking and documenting the 
recorded polarity of nine axis accelerometer head arrays and head angular rate sensors (ARS) 
relative to NHTSA sign convention. Documenting the polarity of channels before use serves to 
increase the confidence that they will record data correctly during an event. The polarities in this 
document are the same as those of the SAE J211 and SAE J1733. 
 
4.1 NINE AXIS ACCELEROMETER HEAD ARRAY 
 
One approach to check the polarity of the head nine-axis accelerometers is to strike the dummy’s 
head with a rubber mallet from various directions to induce a measurable acceleration. 
 
• Striking the dummy head from the rear should result in a positive Ax. 
• Striking the dummy head from the left side should result in a positive Ay  
• Striking the dummy head from the top should result in a positive Az. 
 
If any of these striking motions do not result in a positive reading, the polarity needs to be 
changed to agree with the sign convention. A sign change in the software may be the simplest 
solution. 
 
Following this approach, it is possible to determine the polarity of each nine axis accelerometer 
data channel in the dummy head. 
 
Polarity Check Data Sheet for Head Nine Axis Accelerometer Rate Sensors 
Dummy Type:  
Serial No.:  
Date: 
Direction 
Action 
Polarity 
Ax 
Strike rear of dummy head 
+ (positive) 
Ay 
Strike left side of dummy head 
+ (positive) 
Az 
Strike top of dummy head 
+ (positive) 
Table G1: Polarity Check Data Sheet for Head Nine Axis Accelerometer Rate Sensors 
An alternate approach to determine the polarity of the accelerometers mounted in the dummy 
head uses the constant force of gravity as the input. This procedure will yield the same polarity 
as the previous procedure. Since the sign convention is fixed with respect to the dummy, this 
procedure can be conducted outside the test vehicle on the laboratory floor or table, but the 
dummy must be attached to the data acquisition system. 
 
The procedure for each channel requires placing the accelerometers to be checked perpendicular 
to the axis of gravity in two orientations, each 180 degrees apart, and recording the sign and 


## Page 313

G7 
value of the acceleration channel due to the earth’s gravity for a short period of time. The 
SA572-S4 accelerometer is defined as perpendicular to the axis of gravity when the plane 
containing both mounting screw holes is perpendicular to the force of gravity. See Figure G4. 
 
 
Figure G4: SAE 572-S4 Accelerometer Perpendicular to the Force of Gravity in Two 
Orientations 180 Degrees Apart 
 
When the SAE 572-S4 accelerometer is mounted in a plane perpendicular to the force of gravity 
the orientation of the dummy head having the most positive output for that accelerometer 
channel defines positive polarity when moved away from the earth center. The polarity must 
agree with the SAE J211 sign convention. 
 
The data collected should be recorded in the Polarity Check Data Sheet respectively for the x, y, 
and z accelerometers (Tables G2, G3, and G4 below). As an example, refer to the Polarity 
Check Data Sheet, Table G2, for documenting the x-axis polarity.  
 
To determine the polarity of the head x accelerometer:  
1. Lay the dummy face down (FD) and record the x-accelerometer’s output in g’s in 
the appropriate column. 
2. Then place the dummy face up (FU) and record the channel output in g’s in the 
appropriate column. 
3. List the orientation of the most positive value in the next column, either FD or 
FU, paying attention to the sign from the data acquisition system (-1 is more 
positive than -2 g’s). 
4. Next, compare the orientation of the most positive value with the J211 orientation 
for positive sign convention. 
a. If the dummy’s orientation of the most positive value is consistent with 
that of the J211 sign convention, then the channel output will be in 
accordance with the sign convention. 
b. If, however, the dummy’s orientation of the most positive value is 
different than that of the J211 sign convention, then the channel’s output 
will have to be reversed by the data acquisition software in order to be in 
accordance with the sign convention. 


## Page 314

G8 
5. Place a check in the column titled “Negative Channels to Be Reversed in Data 
Acquisition System” for those channels that will require reversal by the data 
acquisition software. 
 
The procedure for the y-axis accelerometers is similar to that used for the x-axis and can be 
accomplished on a floor or bench surface. In this instance, the dummy is placed on its side in two 
different orientations - one where the right shoulder is down (RSD) and one where the right 
shoulder is up (RSU). Once again, all of the channels can be recorded at one time. Then, flip the 
dummy onto its other side and record the values again. List the orientation of the most positive 
value and compare that with that J211 orientation for positive sign convention. Indicate the 
channels to be reversed, if any. 
 
For the z-axis, turning the larger adult dummies over and standing them on their heads is quite 
difficult. Thus, for the z-axis check, it is recommended to secure the dummy in a chair, seat it 
upright and then rotate the dummy in the chair forward or backward about 60 degrees. The force 
on the accelerometer varies with the cosine of the angle it makes with respect to tangent to the 
earth’s surface. 
 
With the dummy sitting upright (U) in the chair, record the z-axis accelerometer channel outputs 
in the appropriate column on the Polarity Check Data Sheet. Next, lean the dummy forward or 
backward approximately 60 degrees and record the z-axis accelerometer outputs in the column 
labeled “Lean Down.” It should be noted that the symbol “D” (for down) has been associated 
with this orientation. Again, follow the procedure outlined for the x-axis and y-axis 
accelerometers to complete the z-axis Polarity Check Data Sheet. 
 
 
Table G2: Polarity Check Data Sheet for X Nine Axis Accelerometers 
 


## Page 315

G9 
 
 
Table G3: Polarity Check Data Sheet for Y Nine Axis Accelerometers 
 
Table G4: Polarity Check Data Sheet for Z Nine Axis Accelerometers 


## Page 316

G10 
4.2 HEAD ANGULAR RATE SENSORS (ARS) 
 
To check the polarity of the head ARS, the head and chest must be moved in opposite directions 
to induce a measurable rotational rate.  
 
• Moving the right ear toward the right shoulder should result in a positive ωx.  
• Moving the chin away from the sternum should result in a positive ωy 
• Moving the chin towards the right shoulder should have a positive ωz. 
 
If any of these motions do not result in a positive reading, the polarity needs to be changed to 
agree with the sign convention. A sign change in the software may be the simplest solution. 
 
Polarity Check Data Sheet for Head Angular Rate Sensors 
Dummy Type:  
Serial No.  
Date:

Motion 
Polarity 
ωx 
Rotate right ear toward right shoulder 
+ (positive) 
ωy 
Rotate chin away from sternum 
+ (positive) 
ωz 
Rotate chin toward right shoulder 
+ (positive) 
Table G5: Polarity Check for Head Angular Rate Sensors 
5. UPPER AND LOWER NECK LOAD CELLS 
 
To check the polarity of the upper neck load cells, the head and chest must be moved in opposite 
directions to make a measurable force in the neck. See Figure G5 below. 
 
• Moving the head rearward and the chest forward should result in a positive Fx. 
• Moving the head leftward and the chest rightward should result in a positive Fy. 
• Lifting the head upward and the chest downward should result in a positive Fz.

cells.

• Moving the chin toward the sternum results in a positive My. 
• Moving the chin toward the left shoulder will have a positive Mz.

6. UPPER AND LOWER TIBIA LOAD CELLS 
 
To check the polarity of the upper tibia load cell forces and moments (for each leg), the tibiae 
and femurs must be moved to induce measurable forces and moments.  
 
• Moving the tibia downward and the femur upward should result in a positive Fz. 
• Moving the tibia leftward while holding the knee in place should result in a positive Mx. 
• Moving the tibia forward while moving the bottom of the knee clevis rearward should 
result in a positive My.

4. 
OTHER LOAD CELL BARRIERS ........................................................................................ 4 
 
 


## Page 326

H2 
1. PURPOSE 
 
In conjunction with NHTSA’s research activities, frontal NCAP tests may be used as a means of 
collecting data through load cells mounted to the rigid barrier wall. In these cases, an array of 
load cells may be provided to the contractor. The Contractor may also be asked to furnish one if 
available. The following sections describe some typical load cell wall arrangements. 
 
At the COR’s discretion, the Contractor may be instructed to use a plain plywood barrier face 
rather than one of the load cell arrangements below. In these cases, a 1.5 inch thick depth of 
plywood (fashioned from two sheets of ¾” plywood bonded together) should be mounted to the 
face of the barrier. 
 
A Contractor-supplied load cell barrier may be allowed to deviate from the below specifications 
if those deviations have been previously approved by the COR. 
 
2. 36 LOAD CELL BARRIER WALL 
 
NHTSA may furnish, or ask that the contractor furnish, a load cell barrier wall that contains 36 
load cells, 250 mm x 250 mm nominal in size, arranged in 4 rows of 9 load cells in each as 
shown in Figure 1H. The load cells are single-axis and record force in the x-direction (Fx). Each 
load cell shall be faced with plywood blocks that are 250 mm x 250 mm square and 1.5 in thick 
(fashioned from two sheets of ¾” plywood bonded together). The gap between the load cell wall 
and the floor should be as close to, but no more than, 80 mm (3.15 in). The struck surfaces shall 
be flat and square.  
 
An 18 x 83-in extension, provided by the Contractor, shall be added to the top of the load cell 
barrier wall as shown in Figure 1H to prevent vehicle hood override. The rigid steel frame shall 
be faced with plywood 1.5 in thick. The overall height and width of this barrier configuration 
should be, at a minimum, the size of the high resolution 176 load cell barrier illustrated in 
Section 3 of this appendix.  
 
The struck plywood surfaces shall be flat and square. The contractor is responsible for 
maintaining the plywood facing on the load cells and the extension, including the fabrication and 
replacement of any damaged plywood. The contractor shall replace any sections of the plywood 
facing at the COR’s request. 
 


## Page 327

H3 
 
Figure 1H: Load Cell Locations on a 36-Load Cell Barrier with Plywood Height Extension 
 
3. HIGH RESOLUTION 176 LOAD CELL BARRIER WALL 
 
NHTSA may also furnish a load cell wall that contains 176 load cells, 125 mm x 125 mm 
nominal in size, arranged in 11 rows of 16 load cells in each as shown in Figures 2H and 3H. 
Each load cell shall be faced with plywood blocks that are 125 mm x 125 mm square and 1.5 in 
thick (fashioned from two sheets of ¾” plywood bonded together).  
 
The load cells are multi-axis and record force in the x-direction (Fx) as well as moments about 
the y-axis and z-axis (My and Mz, respectively). The Contractor may be directed by the COR to 
collect data from this load cell wall in the following ways: 
 
1. Fx, My, and Mz on all rows; up to 528 channels total 
2. Fx on all rows, My and Mz on rows G-J; up to 304 channels total 
3. Fx only; up to 176 channels total 
 
The nominal size of the load cell barrier wall with plywood facing should be 2000 mm wide by 
1375 mm tall. The gap between the load cell wall and the floor should be as close to, but no 
more than, 80 mm (3.15 in).  
 
The struck plywood surfaces shall be flat and square. The contractor is responsible for 
maintaining the plywood facing on the load cells, including the fabrication and replacement of 
any damaged plywood. The contractor shall replace any sections of the plywood facing at the 
COR’s request. 


## Page 328

H4 
 
 
Figure 2H: Dimensions of a 176-Load Cell High Resolution Barrier Mounting Structure 
 
 
 
Figure 3H: High Resolution 176 Load Cell Barrier Mounting Locations 
 
4. OTHER LOAD CELL BARRIER WALLS 
 
At the COR’s request, any Contractor-owned load cell barrier wall for full frontal NCAP testing 
may be installed. The load cell barrier wall must be, at a minimum, the height and width of the 
impact face of the high resolution 176 load cell barrier presented in Section 3 of this appendix. 
The COR may request a schematic of a laboratory’s load cell barrier wall prior to allowing its 
use in NCAP testing.

## Page 331

I1 
1. TEST DELIVERABLES AND REPORTING REQUIREMENTS 
 
 
MONTHLY STATUS REPORTS 
 
The contractor shall submit a Monthly Vehicle Status Report to the COTR no later than 
the 15th day of each month following the month being reported on. The form can be 
found in Section 3, Forms, in this appendix. The report shall be submitted until all 
vehicles or items of equipment are disposed of. 
 
 
APPARENT TEST FAILURE 
 
An apparent test failure, as described by Section 13 of the main test procedure, shall be 
communicated by telephone to the COTR within 24 hours with written notification 
emailed within 48 hours (Saturday and Sundays excluded). A Laboratory Notice of Test 
Failure (located in Section 3, Forms, of this appendix) with a copy of related NCAP test 
data sheet(s) and preliminary data plot(s) shall be included.  
 
In the event of a test failure, a post-test calibration check of some of the critically 
sensitive test equipment and instrumentation may be required for verification of accuracy. 
The necessity for the calibration shall be at the COTR’s discretion and shall be performed 
without additional costs to the Office of Crashworthiness Standards (OCWS). 
 
 
NCAP TEST DELIVERABLES 
 
Required deliverables for each test are discussed in this section. A Schedule of 
Deliverables is also provided at the end of this section  
 
A. 
QUICKLOOK REPORT 
 
The Quicklook Report is a preliminary summary of the test that should be e-mailed 
to the OCWS within 24 hours of the impact event. The Quicklook Report should 
detail all relevant injury criteria, vehicle information, air bag deployment, and 
evidence of FMVSS No. 208, FMVSS No. 212, FMVSS No. 219, FMVSS No. 301, 
and FMVSS No. 305 (if applicable) performance, and should include relevant data 
traces. Also, anything interesting or out of the ordinary should be included in the 
Quicklook Report comments section. A sample Quicklook Report is included as 
Form 5 in Section 4 of this appendix. 
 
B. 
DATA TAPE 
 
Within three (3) working days of the test, the Contractor shall email or upload to the 
FTP site the test data formatted using NHTSA’s software and test data formatting 
guidelines. 
 


## Page 332

I2 
The software may be found in the Downloads area at 
https://www.nhtsa.gov/databases-and-software/entree-windows. Select the latest 
version of the program to download and use. 
 
The formatting guide may also be found at https://www.nhtsa.gov/databases-and-
software/entree-windows under NHTSA Test Reference Guides. The latest revision 
to Volume I: Vehicle Tests should be used. 
 
Any questions pertaining to this software should be directed to NCAP COR or to 
the following technical support department: 
 
U.S. Dept. of Transportation 
NHTSA/NVS-300 
W46-318 
1200 New Jersey Ave SE 
Washington, DC 20590 
 
C. 
QUALITY CONTROL PACKAGE  
 
The Quality Control Package is a .zip file that includes all the information 
necessary for NHTSA’s quality control review. It serves as a summary of the test 
and includes, organized by folders labelled appropriately:  
 
 
the test data (data tape) 
o per Section 1.3, A of this appendix  
 
photographs, 
o labeled in order per Section 2.3 of this appendix 
o “Impact for the web” photo – 710 x 410 pixels, landscape orientation 
 
videos  
o high speed videos per Section 9.1 of the main frontal test procedure 
o real-time videos per Section 9.1 of the main frontal test procedure 
o documentation video per Sections 9.7 and 9.8 of the main frontal test 
procedure 
 
pre- and post-test dummy qualification data 
o per guidelines in appropriate appendices  
 
Report of Vehicle Condition 
o Form 2 of this appendix  
 
a copy of the Quicklook Report previously e-mailed to the OCWS 
o per Section 1.3, A of this appendix 
 
The Quality Control Package should be uploaded to the FTP site within five (5) 
business days of the test for review by the OCWS. Providing this data in a timely 
manner will ensure that the Contractor and the COR will be able to discuss the 
details of both test conduct and report content soon after the test is conducted. The 
filename for the Quality Control Package should be formatted as follows: 
 
<NHTSANO><Model Year><Make & Model><Body><NCAP>QC.zip 


## Page 333

I3 
 
The contractor will also provide website-related material in a folder within this file. 
The contractor will provide a .jpg image of the vehicle impact appropriate for use 
on the website. This photo should be a duplicate of photo number 78 in the Frontal 
NCAP photo list found in Section 3 of this appendix. The photo should be labeled 
as follows: 
 
<Model Year><Make><Model>Frontal Impact Event for web.jpg 
 
It should also be 710 pixels wide by 410 pixels tall, landscape (horizontal) 
orientation, and of a high image quality. 
 
Camera No. 1, the Real-Time Left Overall Camera, as described in Section 9 of the 
main procedure, should be provided in .wmv format so it may serve as a web-ready 
video of the impact event in.  
 
D. 
PRELIMINARY (DRAFT) TEST REPORT 
 
Contractors are required to submit to the OCWS via e-mail a Draft Test Report, an 
electronic copy in .pdf or .doc form, within two calendar weeks of the test. If the 
electronic file is larger than 20 MB, the Contractor should upload the file to the FTP 
site instead.  
 
<NHTSANO><Model Year><Make & Model><Body><NCAP>DraftReport.pdf 
 
The Contractor should use detailed descriptions of all test events. Any events that 
are associated with the pass/fail of indicant FMVSS No. 208, FMVSS No. 212, 
FMVSS No. 219, or FMVSS No. 301 testing, or that are of technical interest should 
also be included. Events associated with the pass/fail of indicant FMVSS No. 305 
testing (if applicable) should also be included. 
 
Contractors are required to review and proofread all test reports before submittal to 
the COR. The OCWS will not act as a report quality control office for contractors. 
Reports containing a significant number of errors will be returned to the Contractor 
for correction and a hold will be placed on invoice payment for that test. The 
OCWS will alert the Contractor to any minimal corrections that should be made 
prior to submission of the Final Test Report. 
 
E. 
FINAL TEST REPORT AND DELIVERABLES 
 
The Final Test Report and associated documentation, including test data, properly 
labeled and numbered photographs and videos (including documentation, high-
speed, real-time, and those for the web), are relied upon as the chronicle of the 
NCAP test. Each Final Test Report should also be a complete document capable of 
standing by itself. 
 


## Page 334

I4 
The Final Test Report and associated deliverables will be released to the public 
domain after review and acceptance by the COTR. For these reasons, all 
deliverables must be complete and error-free. Final Test Reports containing errors 
will be returned to the Contractor for correction and a hold will be placed on the 
invoice payment for that test. 
 
NOTE: Only those photos required in the Final Test Report, as set forth in this 
procedure, shall be included unless the OCWS requests the inclusion of 
additional photos to document specific test events or anomalies.  
 
The Contractor shall upload the Final Test Report and final versions of the 
associated test data, photos, and videos as a .zip file to the FTP site within two (2) 
weeks of receiving data tape and Draft Test Report corrections from the OCWS. 
The format for its filename should be as follows: 
 
<NHTSANO><Model Year><Make & Model><Body><NCAP>FinalDeliverables.zip

REPORT AREA 1: PURPOSE AND SUMMARY OF TEST 
 
PURPOSE 
 
This area briefly outlines the purpose for conducting the frontal impact test and states the 
appropriate test procedure followed during the test. The following language is provided as an 
example: 
 
This «Speed» km/h frontal barrier impact test is part of the Vehicle Barrier Impact 
Testing Program sponsored by the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration 
(NHTSA) under Contract No. DTNHXX-XX-D-XXXXX. The purpose of this test was to 
obtain vehicle crashworthiness and occupant restraint system performance data for 
consumer information purposes. 
 
The «Speed» km/h frontal barrier impact test was conducted in accordance with the 
Office of Crashworthiness Standards Laboratory Procedure for NCAP Full Frontal Rigid 
Barrier Impact Testing. 
 
SUMMARY 
 
A load cell barrier consisting of # load cells was impacted by a «Year» «Make» «Model» 
«BodyStyle» at a velocity of «Speed» km/h. The test was performed at XXX Engineering 
on «Date». Pre- and post-test photographs of the vehicle and dummies can be found in 
Appendix A. 
 
One real-time camera and 16 high-speed cameras were used to document the frontal 
barrier impact event. Camera locations and other pertinent camera information can be 
found in this report. 
 
One Part 572E 50th percentile male anthropomorphic test device (ATD) was placed in 
the driver position and one Part 572O 5th percentile female ATD was placed in the right-
front passenger position according to dummy placement instructions specified in the 
Laboratory Procedure for NCAP Full Frontal Rigid Barrier Impact Testing. 
 


## Page 343

I13 
Both ATDs were fully instrumented with head, chest and pelvis tri-axial accelerometers, 
chest displacement potentiometers, upper neck transducers, femur load cells, and lower 
leg instrumentation. Seat belt load cells were installed on the driver's and passenger's lap 
and shoulder belts to measure dummy torso and pelvic section loading.  
 
The driver (position 1) ATD (Serial No. «P1SNo») and the right-front passenger 
(position 2) ATD (Serial No. «P2SNo») were qualified prior to this test. Certification 
details, along with instrumentation calibration data, are found in Appendix C of this 
report. 
 
The «DataCh» channels of data were recorded on an on-board data acquisition system. 
Appendix B contains the vehicle, load cell barrier and dummy response data traces. 
 
There was 100 percent windshield retention and no intrusion into the protected zone of 
the windshield during the event. There was no Stoddard solvent leakage {or electrolyte 
spillage} after the event or during any phase of the static rollover.  
 
The maximum static crush of the vehicle was «MaxCrush» mm and both the driver and 
passenger side doors remained closed during the impact event and were operable after 
the impact. 
 
The driver’s visible contact points were as follows: XXXXXX. The passenger’s visible 
contact points were as follows: XXXXXX. 
 
The occupant data is summarized below:

Data sheets can be found in Section 3 of this appendix. For purposes of consistency, it is 
highly suggested that exact replicas of these sheets are inserted into the Final Test Report. 
The Contractor may expand upon the data sheets if desired; however, the data must be

REPORT AREA 3: PHOTOGRAPHIC DOCUMENTATION (TEST REPORT 
APPENDIX A) 
 
The following photographs should be included as Appendix A of the final test report, two 
photos per page. A vehicle information placard, identifying the test vehicle, test date, and 
NHTSA number, along with an indication of whether the photo was taken pre-test or post-
test, shall clearly appear in each photograph. In cases where it may be unreasonable to 
include this long form placard, an indication of NHTSA number should suffice. A time/date 
stamp on each photo is also highly recommended.  
 
The following photographs should be included with the Quality Control Package and labeled 
as indicated. The text in parenthesis is for clarification purposes only and need not be 
included. If additional photographs are need to satisfy the requirements of report Appendix 
A, including but not limited to photographs required for indicant FMVSS 305 testing, 
subsequent photos should be lettered and labeled appropriately. 
 
Additional photographs which further describe what is visible in Photograph Nos. 1 – 79 
should be labeled with the most relevant photograph number followed by a, b, c, etc. 
 
For example, if the laboratory would like to provide more than one photograph of the dummy 
cable routing configuration pre-test, the photographs should be labeled as follows: 
 
027 – Pre-test Dummy Cable Routing (required photo) 
027a – Pre-test Dummy Cable Routing (additional view) 
 
Any additional photographs taken for documentation of vehicle anomalies, safety concerns, 
test details, etc. which do not fit under the photograph descriptions above should be 
appropriately labeled and shall follow the list of preceding required photographs in numerical 
order. 
 
No. 01 
Load Cell Location (photograph of vehicle behind mock load cell wall) 
No. 02 
Pre-Test Load Cell Wall 
No. 03 
Post-Test Load Cell Wall 
No. 04

be seen clearly without glare or blurring) 
No. 05

without glare or blurring, include a photograph of the reduced load carrying 
capacity as No. 005a, if applicable)

should also be uploaded to the FTP site along with the Quality Control Package. 
 
 
REPORT AREA 6: TEST EQUIPMENT AND INSTRUMENTATION CALIBRATION 
(TEST REPORT APPENDIX D)

data, should be provided as Appendix D of each vehicle Final Test Report. Appendix D 
should identify all test equipment, dummy sensors, potentiometers, and load cells used to 
collect data during the test. Calibration dates for each should be provided as indicated in 
the sample tables below. Comments should also be included, if appropriate.

3. DATA SHEETS 
 
Data sheets are provided as tools to document test data in the final test report format as outlined 
in Section 2 of this appendix. The Contractor is not restricted from using other tools or 
expanding the data sheets provided in this section. Nevertheless, for consistency and uniformity 
in reporting data, the Contractor should present the data in the order outlined in this section.

compliant.

Ri2 = Ro (1 + V1/V2) [(V2-V2’)/V2’]

## Page 393

I63 
4. FORMS 
 
Forms, like Data Sheets, are provided as tools to use in the exchange of data between the 
COR and the Contractor. Forms, unlike Data Sheets, are not part of the Final Test 
Report. The Contractor is not restricted from using other tools or expanding the forms 
outlined in this section. 
 
 
A. 
FORM 1 – Test Vehicle Information 
 
A “Test Vehicle Information” form will be supplied, either by the purchasing 
Contractor or the COR, to the Contractor before testing preparation. Information 
on this form is supplied by the automobile manufacturer to aid in the initial test 
setup and shall be considered as reference material. After vehicle preparation is 
complete, the Test Vehicle Information form shall be discarded. 
 
 
B. 
FORM 2 – Report of Vehicle Condition 
 
A “Report of Vehicle Condition” form must be submitted to the COR.  The first 
page of the form shall be completed when the test vehicle arrives at the testing 
laboratory. The second page of the form is completed after the test and submitted 
with the Quality Control Package. The forms shall be legible (handwritten forms 
are unacceptable) and complete (all information requested is filled out). 
 
 
C. 
FORM 3 – Laboratory Notice of Invalid Test or Apparent Test Failure 
 
A “Laboratory Notice of Invalid Test or Apparent Test Failure” form will be 
submitted to the NHTSA COR to report either an invalid test or a test failure. The 
invalid test or potential failure shall be described thoroughly in the spaces 
provided. 
 
 
D. 
FORM 4 – Monthly Status Reports 
 
a. Form 4a: Vehicle Inventory Report  
The purpose of a “Vehicle Inventory Report” is to track all vehicles tested 
under NCAP and in the Contractor’s possession. It should contain all NCAP-
owned, optional, and lab-owned retest vehicles. The information should be 
organized in an Excel file format according to the structure described by 
Form 4a and submitted to the COR each month (no later than the 15th of the 
month following the reporting month) until all vehicles have been discarded. 
An alternative schedule may be used if approved by the COR. A sample 
template will be provided by the COR. 
 
b. Form 4b: Invoicing Report 
The “Invoicing Report” allows NHTSA to identify and reconcile its internal 
invoicing records against the Contractor’s. The information should be 
organized in an Excel file format according to the structure outlined under 


## Page 394

I64 
Form 4b and submitted to the COR each month (no later than the 15th of the 
month following the reporting month). A sample template will be provided by 
the COR. 
 
c. Form 4c: ATD and Sensor Inventory Report 
An “ATD and Sensor Inventory Report,” in Excel file format and according to 
the structure outlined under Form 4c, shall be submitted to the COR either 
monthly (no later than the 15th of the month following the reporting month) or 
upon request, depending on the section of the “ATD and Sensor Inventory 
Report” in question. An alternative schedule may be used if approved by the 
COR. A sample template will be provided by the COR. 
 
 
E. 
FORM 5 - Quicklook Report 
 
A “Quicklook Report” of pertinent test data, as described in Section 1.3, A of this 
appendix, should be prepared and sent via e-mail to pertinent NHTSA personnel 
within twenty-four (24) hours of test completion. 
 
F. 
FORM 6 - Vehicle Air Bag and Restraint Deactivation and Removal 
 
A “Vehicle Air Bag and Restraint Deactivation and Removal” form should be 
completed and submitted to the COR within 14 days of receiving authorization to 
complete restraint deactivation activities.

____________________________________________________________________ 
 
NCAP will also remove the following parts if the target test weight cannot be achieved: 
 
Frontal NCAP test: spare tire, rear door windows, rear radio speakers, interior door 
trim on the rear doors, rear seat cushions, outboard mirrors, tail lights, rear bumper 
 
Side NCAP tests: spare tire, rear radio speakers, interior door trim and windows on 
non-struck side, outboard mirrors on non-struck side, taillights, rear bumper 
 
Please prioritize the items in this list in order of removal preference for each NCAP test. 
Please make a note of any parts that should not be removed because they serve as load 
bearing or structural components and therefore, will likely affect NCAP test performance. 
Also, please feel free to add additional items which are not listed if their removal is 
deemed acceptable.

FORM 4a - VEHICLE INVENTORY REPORT 
 
Each month, the Contractor should provide the COR with a report of the NCAP-related vehicles 
they have in inventory. This should include NCAP-owned, optional, and lab-owned retest 
vehicles. If the Contractor is in possession of vehicles that are associated with more than one 
NCAP contract, each tab in the file should only include details related to one contract number. 
Each tab should be named using the contract number along with an indication of the test 
direction (e.g., front or side). The chart below should be recreated in an Excel file with data 
added according to the chart key below. 
 
The Excel file name should be structured as follows: 
 
< 3 Letter Lab Name/TSTPRF><Year><Month>Form 4a Vehicle Inventory Report.xlsx 
 
All columns shown below must be included, in the same order shown. Additional columns of 
pertinent information may be added to (but not inserted in between) these columns. 
 
No.

to? 
1 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
2 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Chart Key: 
 
 No.: Sequential number identifying each vehicle purchased under the contract. 
 Test Mode: Indicate the type of crash test performed on the vehicle: frontal, side MDB, 
or side pole 
 Year/Make/Model: Indicate the year, make, and model of the vehicle 
 NHTSA No.: Indicate the vehicle’s NHTSA number 
 Owner: Indicate the owner of the NCAP vehicle 
 VIN: Indicate the vehicle’s 17-digit identification number (VIN) 
 Delivery Date: Indicate the date the vehicle was received at your laboratory 
 Crash Test Date: Indicate the date the vehicle was subject to crash testing. 
 Final Odometer: Indicate the final odometer reading just prior to releasing or 
transferring the vehicle out of your possession 
 Restraints Deactivated?: Indicate “no” in this field until instructions are received from 
the COR to deactivate all of the vehicle restraints. After those activities are completed, 
indicate “yes.” 
 Vehicle Disposal Date: Indicate the date the vehicle is transferred out of your 
possession. 
 Transferred to?: Indicate the recipient of the vehicle once is it transferred out of your 
possession. 
 


## Page 415

I85 
FORM 4b – INVOICING REPORT 
 
Each month, the Contractor should supply the COR with a report of current invoicing activities.  
 
The Excel file name should be structured as follows: 
< 3 Letter Lab Name/TSTPRF><Year><Month>Form 4b Invoicing Report.xlsx 
 
If the Contractor is invoicing items on multiple NCAP contracts, each tab in the Excel file should only include details related to one 
contract number. Each tab should be named using the contract number along with an indication of the test direction (e.g., front or 
side). 
 
The header and chart information detailed below should be replicated for each separate delivery order issued under the contract, so 
that all delivery orders issued under a contract are contained on one tab in the Excel file. The lab should construct a completely new 
chart for each delivery order issued under a contract based on the items included in each subsequent delivery order. 
 
All header items and chart columns shown below must be included, in the same order shown. Additional chart columns of pertinent 
information may be added to (but not inserted in between) these chart columns. For ease of discussion, the “left” and “right” sides of 
the chart are discussed separately. Spreadsheets should be designed according to the header, “left,” and “right” chart keys below. 
 
In addition to building in the calculations and functionality described throughout the following sections, the Contractor should use 
conditional formatting or other functions in Excel to flag or highlight information that could lead to problems such as invoicing more 
contract line item numbers (CLINs) than were ordered or charging the incorrect price. 
 
Header Key: 
 
Contract No: DTNH221XD00XXX 
 
Delivery Order: DTNH221XF00XXX 
DO PoP Start Date:
12/11/2016 
Total Award:
$5,000.00
Requisition No: DTNH221XRQ0XXX 
DO PoP End Date:
12/10/2017 
Invoiced:
$4,200.00
 
PoP Extension End Date:
6/10/2018 
Balance:
$800.00
 
 Contract No: Place the contract number in a larger font at the top left corner of the sheet. This should be duplicated towards 


## Page 416

I86 
the top left corner of each delivery order chart generated on the tab. 
 Delivery Order: Delivery order number. 
 Requisition No: Requisition number. 
 DO PoP Start Date: The start date for the delivery order’s period of performance (PoP). 
 DO PoP End Date: The end date for the delivery order’s period of performance (PoP). 
 PoP Extension End Date: The new period of performance end date (PoP) if the delivery order end date has been extended. 
 Total Award: The total funds awarded on the delivery order. 
 Invoiced: Subtotal of items invoiced on the delivery order thus far. This field should contain a function to calculate the sum of 
the Line Total column described under “Left” Chart Key below. 
 Balance: The remaining funds on the delivery order. This field should contain a function to calculate the difference between 
Total Award and Invoiced.

functional and sum the Total fields from the “Right Side” of the spreadsheet. 
 Comments: Comments related to this test item that are relevant to the invoicing process.

 “Right Side” of Chart 
 
The columns on the “right side” of the spreadsheet are more dynamic than the “left side” columns. For each new delivery order, a 
different set of contract line item numbers (CLINs) will be included. For each CLIN contained on a delivery order, a block of specific 
information should be placed to the right of the information described in the “Left Side” section above. The number of these blocks 
depends on the variety of CLINs included on a delivery order. In turn, this dictates how many columns will need to be summed to 
propagate the Line Total field described in the “Left Side” section. 
 
Each line under this heading block is aligned with a Test Item line from the “Left” side of the chart. The following is an example of 
the column and field headers needed for each block:

 CLIN Description and Number: Each block should be titled with a description of the CLIN and its associated number 
 Unit Price: The unit price for the subject CLIN. 
 Qty (Quantity) Ordered: The number of items ordered under the subject CLIN on the delivery order. 
 Qty (Quantity) Balance: The remaining number of items under the subject CLIN. This field should contain a function to 
calculate the difference between the sum of the items in the Qty column and the Qty Ordered cell. 
 Qty (Quantity): The total number items under the subject CLIN charged for that Test Item. 
 Total: This field should contain a function to calculate the total cost under the subject CLIN charged for the Test Item, using 
the related Qty and Unit Price fields. All Total cells on a given line should sum to inform the Line Total cell for that Test 
Item. 
 Count: This field should be used to track the quantity of this CLIN used versus the Qty Ordered as reported on the invoice.

FORM 4c – ATD and SENSOR INVENTORY REPORT 
 
Each month, the Contractor should supply the COR with a summary of the NHTSA NCAP GFP 
they have in-house other than test vehicles. This shall include ATDs, sensors, and any other 
equipment that has been provided by NCAP. 
 
The Excel file name should be structured as follows: 
< 3 Letter Lab Name/TSTPRF><Year><Month>Form 4c ATD and Sensor Report.xlsx 
 
Each Excel file should contain at least three tabs. The following sections discuss the structure 
and content of each tab. The Contractor may include additional information in this monthly 
submission, but additional information should be included on subsequent tabs in the spreadsheet. 
 
ATD Inventory Tab 
 
This tab should be labeled “ATDInventory” and contain the following column headers 
describing the NCAP-owned dummies and related equipment (such as head forms and leg forms) 
that the Contractor has in-house: 
 
ATD/Equipment Type Manufacturer
Serial Number

Last

Date 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 ATD/Equipment Type: Describe the type of ATD or equipment 
o eg: Hybrid III 5th, SID IIs, Flex-PLI 
 Manufacturer: Manufacturer of the ATD or equipment 
 Serial Number: Serial number of the ATD or equipment 
 Date In: The date the item was received at the Contractor’s facility 
 Last Qualification Date: The last date the item was qualified

 Sensor Type: Indicate the sensor type. 
o eg: accelerometer, load cell, angular rate sensor 
 Sensor Location: Indicate the ATD location where this sensor is currently installed; 
otherwise, indicate N/A. 
o eg: head, upper neck, pelvis. 
 Manufacturer: Indicate the manufacturer of the sensor. 
 Model: Indicate the model name or number of the sensor. 
 Serial Number: Indicate the serial number of the sensor. 
 Axis: If installed in an ATD along a particular axis, indicate that axis; otherwise, indicate 
N/A. 
 P/R: If installed in an ATD, indicate whether it is in the primary (P) or redundant (R) 
location. 
 Date Received: The date the Contractor received the GFP from NCAP. 
 Date Installed (in ATD): If installed in an ATD, the date the installation occurred. 
 Last Cal Date: The date the sensor was last calibrated. 
 ATD Type: If the sensor is installed in an ATD, indicate the ATD type. Otherwise 
indicate N/A. 
o eg: ES2-re, Hybrid III 3YO 
 ATD S/N: If installed in an ATD, indicate the ATD serial number. Otherwise, indicate 
N/A. 
 
Issue Tracking 
 
The Contractor shall have an internal process for resolving and tracking issues with dummy parts 
and sensors, whether they occur during inspection, qualification, crash testing, SAB-OOP, or 
other activities. Information related to dummy part and sensor issues should be summarized in 
this report on a tab titled “IssueTracking.” 
 
At a minimum, the following information should be recorded: 
NHTSA 
No. 
Make/ 
Model 
Test 
Type 
Test 
Date 
ATD 
Type 
ATD 
S/N
Sensor or 
Part 
Description
Sensor 
or Part 
S/N 
Channel 
No 
Issue Inspection 
Fix/ 
Remedy NOTES
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 NHTSA No: If the entry is tracking a sensor issue that occurred during a vehicle test, 
indicate the NHTSA number of the vehicle. Otherwise, indicate N/A. 
 Make/Model: If the entry is tracking a dummy sensor issue that occurred during a 
vehicle test, indicate the make and model of the vehicle. Otherwise, indicate N/A. 
 Test Type: Indicate the test (or other activity) in which the sensor issue occurred or was 
discovered during. 
o eg: frontal crash test, side pole crash test, neck extension qualification, pre-test 
ATD inspection. 
 ATD Type: Indicate the type of ATD that the sensor was installed in, if any. Otherwise, 
indicate N/A. 


## Page 422

I92 
 ATD S/N: Indicate the serial number of the ATD the sensor is installed in, if any. 
Otherwise, indicate N/A. 
 Sensor or Part Description: Describe the part or sensor exhibiting the issue being 
tracked, including the axis and whether the sensor is primary or redundant, if applicable. 
o eg: head CG primary x accelerometer, upper neck load cell, head skin. 
 Sensor or Part S/N: Indicate the serial number for the sensor or part in question. 
 Channel No.: If the issue occurred during a vehicle test, indicate the channel number in 
the EV5 file. Otherwise, indicate N/A. 
 Issue: Describe the event that initiated the investigation into the sensor or part. 
o eg: noticed during routine inspection, data loss during frontal crash test, ATD 
failed to pass neck extension qualification. 
 Inspection: Describe the results of having inspected the sensor or part. 
o eg: wire found cut, nodding block cracked. 
 Fix/Remedy: Indicate the solution being employed to remedy the sensor or part issue. 
o eg: head skin replaced, accelerometer replaced, re-soldered wire, neck nodding 
blocks replaced. 
 Notes: Include additional information about the issue.
