1. PURPOSE AND APPLICATION 
The New Car Assessment Program’s (NCAP’s) full frontal rigid barrier impact test procedure is 
based on a related safety standard, Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standard (FMVSS) No. 208, 
which specifies performance requirements for the protection of vehicle occupants in crashes. The 
assessment of certain FMVSS-related parameters during NCAP testing allows the Office of 
Crashworthiness Standards (OCWS) to gain supplemental information on the test vehicle. 
 
NOTE: All variables are to be evaluated at NCAP’s 35mph (56.3km/h) full frontal 
rigid barrier test vehicle velocity.  
 
This document is an appendix to the main full frontal rigid barrier laboratory test procedure 
provided by the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration (NHTSA), Office of 
Crashworthiness Standards (OCWS) for the purpose of presenting guidelines for a uniform 
testing data and information recording format, and providing suggestions for the use of specific 
equipment and procedures for contracted testing laboratories. The data correspond to 
requirements for indicant testing in accords with FMVSS No. 212, 219, 301, and 305. The 
OCWS test procedure is not intended to limit or restrain a contractor from developing or utilizing 
any testing techniques or equipment that will assist in procuring the required test data. However, 
applicability of any such testing technique or equipment is subject to prior approval by the COR. 
 
The indicant test procedures presented in this appendix are applicable to vehicles tested under the 
main full frontal rigid barrier NCAP test procedure. It is the contractor’s responsibility to follow 
the most updated versions of all related test procedures when conducting these assessments as 
part of full frontal rigid barrier NCAP testing. These vehicles must also meet the requirements 
set forth in this appendix.  
 
Vehicles will be tested to the requirements contained herein in conjunction with the dynamic 
requirements for full frontal NCAP tests. The test facility must be able to conduct these NCAP 
tests. The facility must meet the minimum requirements regarding weighing capability, speed 
measurement systems, test surface, tow-road, abort system, barriers, and all other requirements. 
 
2. DEFINITIONS 
See main Frontal NCAP Procedure, Section 10 for additional Definitions. 
 
DAYLIGHT OPENING (DLO)  
Maximum unobstructed opening through the glazing surface (windshield), including 
reveal or garnish moldings adjoining the surface, as measured parallel to the outer surface 
of the glazing material. 
 
ELECTROLYTE SPILLAGE 
The fall, flow, or run of propulsion battery electrolyte in, on, or from the vehicle, 
including wetness resulting from capillary action. 
 
FORWARD CONTROL VEHICLE (FCV)  
Configuration in which more than half of the engine length is rearward of the foremost 


## Page 428

J3 
point of the windshield base and the steering wheel hub is in the forward quarter of the 
vehicle length. 
 
PROPULSION BATTERY SYSTEM COMPONENT 
Any part of a propulsion battery module, interconnect, venting system, battery restraint 
device, and battery box or container that holds the individual battery modules used for 
propulsion. 
 
3. PRE-TEST REQUIREMENTS  
3.1. 
DETAILED TEST AND QUALITY CONTROL PROCEDURES REQUIRED 
 
Prior to conducting the indicant test, if requested by the COR, the Contractor may be 
required to submit a detailed in-house test procedure (to the COR) that includes: 
 
a. A step-by-step description of the methodology to be used. 
b. A written Quality Control (QC) Procedure which shall include calibrations, the data 
review process, report review, and the people assigned to perform QC on each task. 
c. A complete listing of test equipment with instrument accuracy and calibration dates. 
d. Detailed check off lists to be used during the test and during data review. These lists 
shall include all test procedure requirements and any additional requirements 
pertaining to the applicable safety standard for which testing is being performed. 
Each separate check off sheet shall identify the laboratory, test date, vehicle, and test 
technicians. These check sheets shall be used to document that all requirements and 
procedures have been complied with. If requested, these sheets shall be submitted 
with the test report. 
e. There shall be no contradiction between the OCWS Laboratory Test Procedure and 
the Contractor's in-house test procedure. 
 
4. FMVSS No. 212 INDICANT TEST 
4.1. 
GENERAL REQUIREMENTS 
This indicant test is based on FMVSS No. 212, which establishes windshield retention 
requirements for motor vehicles during a full frontal rigid barrier test. 
 
When a vehicle is subject to a full frontal rigid barrier NCAP test, the windshield 
mounting of the vehicle shall retain NOT LESS than the minimum portion of the 
windshield periphery as follows: 
 
a. Vehicles equipped with automatic occupant (passive) restraint systems shall retain 
not less than 50% of the portion of the windshield periphery on each side of the 
vehicle longitudinal centerline. 
b. Vehicles NOT equipped with automatic occupant restraint systems shall retain not 
less than 75% of the windshield periphery. 
 


## Page 429

J4 
NOTE: The standard does NOT apply to forward control vehicles, walk-in 
van-type vehicles, or to open-body-type vehicles with fold-down or 
removable windshields. 
 
4.2. 
PROCEDURE 
The following test conditions shall apply: 
 
a. The windshield mounting material and all vehicle components in direct contact 
with the mounting material are at any temperature between –9.4 ºC and 43.3 ºC.  
b. Temperature measurement shall be made 15 minutes before the frontal impact 
test. 
c. Windshield retention must be checked directly after a full frontal rigid barrier 
impact.  
d. Loss of windshield protection can be determined when a piece of paper can pass 
between the windshield edge and the vehicle body. 
e. Photographs of the windshield periphery should be taken before the vehicle is 
placed in the static rollover machine to conduct an FMVSS No. 301 or No. 305 
indicant test. 
 
The Contractor should complete Data Sheet No. 15 in Appendix I to this procedure and 
include it with the test report. 
 
5. FMVSS No. 219 (PARTIAL) INDICANT TEST 
5.1. 
GENERAL REQUIREMENTS 
This indicant test is based on FMVSS No. 219, which specifies limits for the 
displacement of vehicle components into the windshield area during a full frontal rigid 
barrier test. 
 
When a vehicle is subject to a full frontal rigid barrier test as defined by FMVSS No. 
219, no part of the vehicle outside the occupant compartment, except windshield molding 
and other components designed to be normally in contact with the windshield, shall 
penetrate the protected zone to a depth of more than 6 mm (0.25 inch). No such part of 
the vehicle shall penetrate the inner surface of that portion of the windshield within the 
Daylight Opening (DLO) below the protected zone. 
 
The word “partial” is used since the 219 Styrofoam windshield protected zone template is 
eliminated for NCAP 56.3km/h (35mph) full frontal rigid barrier impact tests so the 
driver and passenger dummies can be filmed through the vehicle's windshield. However, 
the lower boundary of the protected zone shall be marked on the windshield glass, and 
any points where a part of the vehicle exterior has marked, penetrated, or broken the 
windshield should be documented, which accounts for a partial standard test.  
 
 
Windshield 
In “Protected Zone” 
Windshield 
Below “Protected Zone” 


## Page 430

J5 
Vehicle Component 
Penetration 
Must not mark, penetrate, or 
break by a part of the vehicle 
exterior 
Must not penetrate inner 
surface of windshield 
 
The windshield must be checked directly after a full frontal rigid barrier impact. 
 
NOTE: The standard does NOT apply to forward control vehicles, walk-in van-type 
vehicles, or to open-body-type vehicles with fold-down or removable 
windshields. 
 
5.2. 
PROTECTED ZONE LOWER EDGE MARKING PROCEDURE 
The lower edge of the protected zone is determined as follows: 
a. Place a 16.5 cm (6.5 in) diameter rigid sphere weighing 6.8 kg (15 lbs) in a 
position such that it simultaneously contacts the inner surface of the windshield 
glazing and the surface of the instrument panel, including padding. If any 
accessories or equipment such as the steering control system obstruct positioning 
of the sphere, remove them, and then replace them prior to barrier impact testing. 
b. Draw the locus of points on the inner surface of the windshield contactable by the 
sphere across the width of the instrument panel. From the outer most contactable 
points, extend the locus line horizontally to the edges of the glazing material.  
 
NOTE: Do not scratch glazing as a method of marking the contact 
between sphere and windshield. 
 
c. Draw a line on the inner surface of the windshield below and a 1.3 cm (0.5 in) 
distance from the locus line. 
d. The lower edge of the protected zone is the longitudinal projection onto the outer 
surface of the windshield on the line determined in item 3. 
 
The Protected Zone is the space enclosed by the following surfaces: 
a. The outer surface of windshield in the pre-crash configuration. 
b. The locus of points 7.6 cm (3 in) outward along perpendiculars drawn to each 
point on the outer surface of the windshield. 
c. The locus of lines forming a 45° angle with the outer surface of the windshield at 
each point along the top and side edges of the outer surface of the windshield and 
the lower edge of the protected zone previously determined, in the plane 
perpendicular to the edge at that point. 
 
The following test conditions shall also apply: 
a. The hood, hood latches, and any other hood retention components are engaged 
prior to the frontal barrier impact test. 
b. Adjustable cowl tops or other adjustable panels in front of the windshield are in 
the position used under normal operating conditions when windshield-wiping 
systems are not in use. 
 


## Page 431

J6 
The Contractor should complete Data Sheet No. 15 in Appendix I to this procedure and 
include it with the test report 
 
6. FMVSS No. 301 INDICANT TEST 
6.1. 
GENERAL REQUIREMENTS 
This indicant test is based on FMVSS No. 301, which specifies performance requirements 
for the integrity of motor vehicle fuel systems. It is the contractor’s responsibility to follow 
the most updated test procedure when conducting this assessment as part of NCAP testing. 
 
1. FRONTAL IMPACT 
When a vehicle is subject to a full frontal rigid barrier NCAP test, the following fuel 
leakage conditions must be met: 
 
TIME 
MAX. FLUID SPILLAGE 
From impact until vehicle motion ceases 
1 ounce by weight 
For 5 minute period after vehicle motion ceases 
5 ounces by weight 
For the next 25 minutes 
1 ounce by weight/minute 
 
2. STATIC ROLLOVER 
After a vehicle is subject to a full frontal rigid barrier NCAP test and placed on a 
static rollover machine, the following fuel leakage conditions must be met: 
 
TIME 
MAX. FLUID SPILLAGE
For 5 minute period from onset of rotation at each 
90° position 
5 ounces by weight 
For 6th minute  
1 ounce by weight 
For 7th minute (if required) 
1 ounce by weight 
For 8th minute (if required) 
1 ounce by weight 
 
6.2. 
FACILITY AND EQUIPMENT – PRE-TEST REQUIREMENTS) 
1. 
STATIC ROLLOVER MACHINE 
The Contractor must have a rollover machine capable of rotating the barrier-
impacted test vehicle about its longitudinal axis with the axis kept horizontal, to 
each successive increment of 90°, 180°, and 270° at a uniform rate, with 90° of 
rotation taking place in any time interval from 1 to 3 minutes.  
 
 
2. 
STODDARD COLLECTION CONTAINERS AND STOPWATCH 
Containers for the collection of Stoddard solvent and a calibrated stopwatch for 
timing the fluid collection intervals are required Leakage will be collected for the 5 


## Page 432

J7 
minute period from the beginning of rotation plus any additional 1 minute 
collection periods that are required. Containers must be labeled before they are 
photographed. 
 
6.3. 
FUEL SYSTEM INTEGRITY PROCEDURE 
After the vehicle impact, fuel system Stoddard solvent leakage (if any) should be 
collected by hand and documented with a real-time (24-30 fps) video camera and 
stopwatch. The “tea cup method” involves simply placing a collection vessel beneath the 
leakage source and timing the intervals of several collected volumes. The collected 
Stoddard solvent samples can subsequently be measured and spillage rates calculated. If 
the “tea cup method” is used, the test personnel must be in position to reach observation 
points around the test vehicle at the instant the vehicle comes to rest after the impact 
event. 
 
 
NOTE: It is the Contractor’s responsibility to collect any suspect liquids 
leaking from the vehicle post-test and analyze the contents if 
necessary. 
 
 
6.4. 
STATIC ROLLOVER PROCEDURE 
Do not proceed to the static rollover in the case of a potentially invalid test, apparent test 
failures, or test anomalies. In those cases, the Contractor should contact the COR for 
instructions on how to proceed.  
 
The Contractor must conduct a static rollover test within 45 minutes after the vehicle 
impact. The Contractor must keep the test vehicle under constant observation for 
Stoddard solvent leakage during the transition between impact and static rollover testing. 
When the test vehicle is rotated in a fixture on its longitudinal axis to each successive 
increment of 90°, following an impact crash, Stoddard solvent spillage, from the onset of 
rotational motion, shall not exceed a total of 5 ounces by weight for the first 5 minutes of 
testing at each successive 90° increment. For the remaining testing period, at each 
increment of 90°, solvent spillage during any l-minute interval shall not exceed 1ounce 
by weight. 
 
6.5. 
STATIC ROLLOVER TEST CONDITIONS 
Prior to conducting any static rollover test, ATDs should be removed from the vehicle. 
Within 45 minutes of vehicle impact, the Contractor should place the vehicle in the test 
fixture, where it may be rotated in a test fixture about its longitudinal axis, with the axis 
kept horizontal, to each successive increment of the following: 
 
Rotation 1 - 90° 
Rotation 2 - 180° 
Rotation 3 - 270° 
Rotation 4 - 360° 
 


## Page 433

J8 
Rotation must take place at a uniform rate, with 90° of rotation taking place in any time 
interval from 1 to 3 minutes. After reaching each 90° increment, the vehicle is held in that 
position for 5 minutes. 
Leakage will be collected for the 5-minute period from the beginning of rotation plus up 
to three 1-minute collection periods. Containers for the collection of possible Stoddard 
solvent spillage and a calibrated stopwatch for timing the fluid collection intervals are 
required. Containers must be labeled before they are photographed. 
 
7.  FMVSS No. 305 INDICANT TEST 
7.1. 
GENERAL REQUIREMENTS 
This indicant test is based on FMVSS No. 305, which specifies performance 
requirements for the limitation of electrolyte spillage, retention of propulsion batteries, 
and electrical isolation of the chassis from the high-voltage system during the crash 
event. It applies to vehicles that use electricity as propulsion power. 
 
It is the contractor’s responsibility to follow the most updated test procedure when 
conducting this assessment as part of NCAP testing. 
 
When a vehicle is subject to a full frontal rigid barrier NCAP test,), it shall NOT: 
a. Spill more than 5.0 liters of electrolyte from propulsion batteries outside the 
passenger compartment, and no visible trace of electrolyte shall spill into the 
passenger compartment. Spillage is measured from the time the vehicle ceases 
motion after a barrier impact test until 30 minutes thereafter, and throughout any 
static rollover after a barrier impact test.  
b. Have any propulsion battery system component located inside the passenger 
compartment move from the location in which they are installed. 
c. Have any propulsion battery system component located outside the passenger 
compartment enter the passenger compartment. 
d. Fail to maintain an electrical isolation of no less than 500 ohms/volt between the 
propulsion battery system and the vehicle’s electricity-conducting structure. 
 
7.2. 
FACILITY AND EQUIPMENT: PRE-TEST REQUIREMENTS 
1. 
VOLTAGE MEASUREMENT DEVICE AND INTERFACE 
The voltmeter used in this test shall measure AC and DC values and have an 
internal impedance of at least 10MΩ. 
 
Voltage measurements throughout this test must be made quickly and safely. To 
ensure these requirements are met, the testing lab must devise, for COTR approval, 
a test interface port or other device to facilitate these voltage measurements. All 
voltage measurements shall be immediate upon connection to the interface port. 
This test interface port equipment shall be easily accessible from the exterior of the 
vehicle and connected to the appropriate propulsion system and battery components 
via laboratory installed wires. The external mounting of this test interface port shall 
be configured such that no movement, interference, or damage will result to it from 


## Page 434

J9 
a barrier crash test. The test interface port shall incorporate a fusible link and any 
other necessary safety device or usage procedure to protect the data measurement 
and recording equipment from damage, and the test technicians from electrical 
shock. 
 
A terminal block or circuit board is recommended as a means to providing an 
external interface  
 
The following is an example quoted from Transport Canada document, “Test 
Procedures, Frontal Impact 208-212-301F-305F, No. 03-002” 
 
“This kit is composed of a PVC box compliant with the electrical code and 
containing insulated banana connectors that allow the measuring equipment to 
be connected for the verification of the standard. A warning light indicates the 
presence of voltage inside the box. A shielded cable with three conductors, 20 
feet in length and capable of supporting 600 volts, connects the box to the 
vehicle’s electrical system. This cable is covered with orange-colored 
mechanical protection (similar to the Hybrid vehicle high-voltage 
identification code). The box is protected by a 0.5-amp fuse.” 
 
2. 
STATIC ROLLOVER MACHINE 
The rollover machine must be capable of rotating, and holding in place, the 
impacted NCAP test vehicle about its longitudinal axis with the axis kept 
horizontal, to each successive increment of 90°, 180°, and 270° at a uniform rate, 
with 90° of rotation taking place in any time interval from 1 to 3 minutes. Leakage 
will be collected for the 5-minute period from the beginning of rotation plus any 
additional 1-minute collection periods that are required. Voltage measurements 
shall be able to be made continuously throughout the rollover test. 
 
3. 
STODDARD AND ELECTROLYTE COLLECTION CONTAINERS AND 
STOPWATCH 
Containers for the collection of Stoddard solvent and propulsion battery electrolyte 
and a calibrated stopwatch for timing the fluid collection intervals are required. 
Containers for each fluid collected must be labeled before they are photographed. 
For containers containing both Stoddard and electrolyte, the fluids should be 
allowed to separate by specific gravity then measured and photographed. 
 
4. 
OTHER TEST INSTRUMENTATION 
The Contractor shall provide the necessary equipment to permanently record and 
display data. The data shall be included in the final test report and on the electronic 
data media. 
 
7.3. 
ELECTROLYTE SPILLAGE AND ELECTRICAL SHOCK PROTECTION PROCEDURE 
1. 
DATA COLLECTION SET-UP  
a. Remove the key from the keylock and ensure the vehicle is not powered.  


## Page 435

J10 
b. Remove barriers to access the propulsion battery module (e.g. seat backs, 
carpet, covers).  
c. Wear high-voltage protection gloves, nonconductive shoes, eye protection 
and any other safety equipment deemed necessary to safely prepare the 
vehicle and conduct the test.  
d. Set the propulsion battery module switch, service plug, or otherwise to the 
“OFF” or depowered, position (See Figure 1J below). Follow any 
Manufacturer instructions provided by the COR. Wait 5 minutes. 
 
 
Figure 1J: Examples of Service Switches and Plugs 
 
e. Remove propulsion battery module service cover, or cover that closes the 
battery compartment.  
f. Measure the voltage across the propulsion battery at the appropriate 
terminals, and verify 0 volts.  
g. Measure the voltage between the positive terminal of the propulsion battery 
and the vehicle body, and verify 0 volts.  
h. Measure the voltage between the negative terminal of the propulsion battery 
and the vehicle body, and verify 0 volts.  
i. If any voltage measurements differ from 0 volts, STOP, quarantine vehicle, 
document incident and contact the COTR.  
j. Attach test leads from the propulsion battery, propulsion system, automatic 
propulsion battery disconnect, ground points, and any other points necessary 
on the vehicle such that immediate retrieval of data is possible after an impact 
event and at all times during the static rollover test. 
 
NOTE: If vehicle is equipped with an automatic disconnect physically 
contained within the battery pack system, all voltage measurements 
after impact will be taken from the traction side of the automatic 
disconnect to the vehicle chassis. 
 
If the vehicle utilizes an automatic disconnect that is not physically 
contained within the battery pack system, all post-impact voltage 
measurements are to be made from the battery side of the automatic 
disconnect. Automatic disconnect presence, location, and set-up 
instruction is vehicle-specific, and is available from the COTR.  
 
Service Plug – Toyota Prius 
 
Service Switch – Honda Civic
Service Switch – Ford Escape


## Page 436

J11 
k. Re-install the propulsion battery module service cover, or otherwise close the 
battery compartment. Take great care to preserve the integrity of the 
connection wiring and propulsion battery hold-downs.  
 
2. 
TEST VEHICLE PREPARATION 
a. Apply paint or other highly visible finish, such as machinist blue, to all 
battery system component attachment fasteners or attachment means (e.g., 
welds), to indicate component movement or separation after the governing 
NCAP barrier test.  
b. If the vehicle is equipped with a liquid cooling system, assure that the coolant 
is a different color than the Stoddard solvent in use. 
c. Reset the propulsion battery module switch, service plug, or otherwise to the 
“ON”, or powered, position. Verify proper function of propulsion system.  
d. Charge the propulsion battery system to:  
 
1. The maximum state of charge recommended by the manufacturer, as 
stated in the vehicle Owner’s Manual, or on a label that is permanently 
affixed to the vehicle; 
OR  
2. A state of charge of not less than 95 percent of the maximum capacity of 
the battery system, if the manufacturer has made no recommendation. 
Maximum capacity can be verified by consulting the COR;  
 OR  
3. The maximum practicable state of charge within the normal operating 
range, as specified by the manufacturer, and as indicated by the vehicle’s 
instrumentation, if the batteries are rechargeable only by an energy source 
on the vehicle. Discuss with COR prior to operating the vehicle.  
e. 
Complete Data Sheets No. 305-1 and No. 305-2 in Appendix I. 
f. 
Prepare the test vehicle per the remainder of this test procedure. 
g. 
Document and photograph the test vehicle per the requirements set forth in 
this test procedure. 
 
3. 
ELECTRICAL ISOLATION BASELINE MEASUREMENT 
NOTE: The following measurements are to be made immediately prior to 
the crash test, and should be completed within 15 minutes. 
 
a. Check that the battery system is connected to the vehicle’s propulsion system, 
and the vehicle is in the “ready-to-drive” (propulsion motor(s) activated) 
position. Start Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix I.  
b. Measure the voltage of the propulsion battery as shown in Figure 2J. Before 
any vehicle impact test, verify that Vb is equal to or greater than the nominal 
operating voltage, as specified by the vehicle manufacturer, or as supplied by 
the COR. If Vb is not equal to or greater than the nominal operating voltage, as 
specified by the vehicle manufacturer, or as supplied by the COR, repeat the 
propulsion battery charging Step d of Item 2 Test Vehicle Preparation and 
promptly call the COR for guidance. The voltmeter used in this test measures 


## Page 437

J12 
direct current values and has an internal impedance of at least 10MΩ. Record 
the voltage measurement as Vb on Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix I. 
Make certain all voltages are DC. If there is AC voltage on the traction side 
connection, consult the COR for additional guidance.

should provide good resolution for the voltage measurements.1

Record this value as Ri / Vb, on Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix I. This 
value must be equal to or greater than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test 
failure has occurred. 
h. If Ri2 is less than Ri1 then, divide Ri2 by the nominal operating voltage of the 
propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5J.  
 
NOTE: If the measured voltage is zero and results in a division by 
zero, record “Zero Volts.” This “zero voltage” condition is 
considered as being compliant.  
 
Record this value as Ri / Vb, on Data Sheet No. 305-3 in Appendix I. This 
value must be equal to or greater than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test 
failure has occurred. 
i. Recheck that the battery system is connected to the vehicle’s propulsion 
system, and that the vehicle in the “ready-to-drive” (propulsion motor(s) 
activated) position.  
j. Verify that the parking brake and transmission are set in accordance with this 
full frontal NCAP procedure.  
k. Perform the full frontal rigid barrier NCAP test.

4. 
ELECTRICAL ISOLATION COMPLIANCE MEASUREMENT 
NOTE: All voltage measurements shall be recorded immediately after the 
governing NCAP barrier impact test, and at the start of each 
increment of 90º, 180º, 270º, and 360º of the FMVSS No. 301 indicant 
static rollover test. 
  
NOTE: If the measured voltage is zero and results in a division by zero, 
record “Zero Volts.” This “zero voltage” condition is considered as 
being compliant.  
  
a. Immediately following the crash test, measure V1, V2, V1 ', and V2 ' voltages per 
Figure 6J with Ro installed and record the values on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix I. 
b. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 5J. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri1 on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix I. 
c. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 6J. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri2 on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix I. 
d. If Ri1 is less than Ri2 then, divide Ri1 by the nominal operating voltage of the 
propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5J. Record this value as Ri / Vb, on 
Data Sheet No. 305-4 in Appendix I. This value must be equal to or greater 
than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has occurred. 
e. 
If Ri2 is less than Ri1 then, divide Ri2 by the nominal operating voltage of the 
propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5J. Record this value as Ri / Vb, on 
Data Sheet No. 305-4 in Appendix I. This value must be equal to or greater 
than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has occurred. 
f. Visually inspect for electrolyte leakage in the passenger compartment and 
record and photograph findings on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in Appendix I. 
Additional photographs to document such findings should be included per the 
requirements set forth in the Photographic Documentation section in 
Appendix I. 


## Page 441

J16 
g. Visually inspect for external battery component entry into the occupant 
compartment and record and photograph findings on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix I. 
h. Visually inspect for internal battery component movement in the occupant 
compartment and record and photograph findings on Data Sheet No. 305-4 in 
Appendix I. Additional photographs to document such findings should be 
included per the requirements set forth in the Photographic Documentation 
section in Appendix I. 
i. Photograph the test vehicle per the deliverables outlined in the governing 
NCAP barrier test procedure and in this test procedure and record any 
additional findings in the applicable data sheets.  
j. Prepare the vehicle for the static rollover test by following Section 6 (FMVSS 
No. 301 Indicant Test) of this appendix. 
 
5. 
ELECTROLYE SPILLAGE PROCEDURE 
 
After the vehicle impact, any propulsion battery electrolyte leakage shall be 
collected by hand and documented with a real time (24 fps) digital video camera. 
Like FMVSS 301 indicant testing, the "tea cup method" may be used to collect 
electrolyte spillage from any leakage source(s), though Contractors are invited to 
suggest alternative methods for fluid collection. The collected propulsion battery 
electrolyte samples can subsequently be measured and spillage volume calculated. 
If the "tea cup method" is used, the test personnel must be in position to reach 
observation points around the test vehicle at the instant the vehicle comes to rest 
after the impact event. If possible, the collections of Stoddard solvent, propulsion 
battery electrolyte, or any other fluids should be segregated (if leakage of fluids is 
present). If it is not possible to collect leakage samples separately, provide a 
collection vessel that is adequately sized to collect the leakage mixture and 
separate by suitable means, post-test. Take adequate safeguards when collecting 
leakage, as it may be hazardous.  
 
The passenger compartment must be visually checked directly after a barrier 
impact for evidence of electrolyte leakage, battery system component intrusion, 
and retention of interior mounted battery modules. There should be no visible 
traces of electrolyte in the passenger compartment. Spillage of battery electrolyte 
outside the passenger compartment, which cannot exceed 5.0 liters, is measured 
from the time the vehicle ceases motion after a barrier impact test until 30 minutes 
thereafter, and throughout any static rollover after a barrier impact test.  
 
Photographs of the propulsion battery system components should be taken before 
the vehicle is placed on the static rollover machine. 
 
6. 
STATIC ROLLOVER TEST AND TEST CONDITIONS 
 
 


## Page 442

J17 
Do not proceed to the static rollover in the case of a potentially invalid test, 
apparent test failures, or test anomalies. In those cases, the Contractor should 
contact the COR for instructions on how to proceed.  
 
The Contractor must conduct a static rollover test within 45 minutes after the 
vehicle impact. The Contractor must keep the test vehicle under constant 
observation for electrolyte leakage during the transition between impact and 
static rollover testing. Any ATDs used for governing NCAP test should also 
be removed prior to the rollover. 
 
 NOTE: When the test vehicle is rotated in a fixture on its longitudinal axis to 
each successive increment of 90o following the full frontal NCAP 
test, propulsion battery electrolyte leakage shall not exceed 5 liters. 
 
Additionally, electrical isolation shall not be less than 500 ohms/volt 
throughout the full frontal NCAP test or at each 90o increment of 
the static rollover test. 
 
a. Reference static rollover preparation and procedure from Section 6 (FMVSS 
No. 301 Indicant Test) of this appendix. 
b. Mount the test vehicle on the static rollover fixture and position at 0o (wheels 
down). 
c. Immediately following the rollover transition of each successive increment of 
90o (e.g. at 90o, 180o, 270o, 360o), perform the following: 
  
NOTE: If measured voltage is zero and results in a division by zero, record 
“Zero Volts.” This “zero voltage” condition is considered as being 
compliant.  
 
i. Measure V1, V2, V1 ', and V2 ' voltages per Figures 3J -6J with Ro 
installed, and record the values on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in Appendix I. 
ii. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 5J. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri1 on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in 
Appendix I. 
iii. Calculate the electrical isolation value (in ohms) as shown in Figure 6J. 
Record the electrical isolation value as Ri2 on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in 
Appendix I. 
iv. If Ri1 is less than Ri2 then, divide Ri1 by the nominal operating voltage of 
the propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5J. Record this value as Ri / 
Vb, on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in Appendix I. This value must be equal to 
or greater than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has 
occurred. 
v. If Ri2 is less than Ri1 then, divide Ri2 by the nominal operating voltage of 
the propulsion battery (Vb) shown in Figure 5J. Record this value as Ri / 
Vb, on Data Sheet No. 305-5 in Appendix I. This value must be equal to 


## Page 443

J18 
or greater than 500. If this value is less than 500, a test failure has 
occurred. 
d. Repeat Step c for increments of 180o, 270o, and 360o. 
 
7. 
POST-ROLLOVER REQUIREMENTS 
a.  After the required tests are completed, the Contractor shall: 
i. Verify all data sheets are complete and take any remaining photographs.  
ii. Complete Form 2 of Appendix I, the Report of Vehicle Condition 
Form, including a word description of the vehicle’s post-test condition. 
iii. Copy applicable pages of the Vehicle Owner’s Manual for attachment to 
the test reports. 
iv. Remove all instrumentation from vehicle. Return vehicle to its pre-test 
condition and move the test vehicle to a secure area.  
v. Place all original records in a secure and organized file to await test data 
disposition.
